## Report on Books for Congress, [23 January] 1783

#### From unknown source

lin’s other works  
  
  
Benjamin Franklin, Political, Miscellaneous, and Philosophical Pieces … (Benjamin Vaughan [1751–1835], comp. and ed., London, 1779). For Vaughan, see Comment by Jefferson, 25 Jan. and n. 1; JM Notes, 19 Mar. 1783, n. 9. The “Vaughan” was the only authorized compilation of Franklin’s works available in 1783. Even Franklin himself probably could not have assembled all his “other works,” including many of concealed authorship, occasional pamphlets, and newspaper ephemerae. That assembling would await twentieth-century scholarship.

## [From _American Publishers' Circular and Literary Gazette (1855-1862)_](https://archive.org/details/sim_american-literary-gazette-and-publishers-circular_1858-07-24_4_30/page/n5/mode/1up?view=theater)

#### 1858-07-24 &middot; [Philadelphia](http://dbpedia.org/resource/Philadelphia)

<table style="width: 100%;"><tr><td style="width: 50%">

  
  
Jeftreys.—A Description of the Spanish  
Islands and Settlements on the Coast of  
the West Indies. Illustrated with 32 maps  
and plans. 4to. hf. cf. Lond., 1762. $3 50.  
  
—— The American Atlas; or, a Geogra-  
phical Description of the Whole Continent

water colors.  
  
Bishop Lightfoot’s literary remains are far more extensive  
than had been expected. He has left an unfinished work on the  
Northumbrian Saints, a much-enlarged edition of ‘‘ Clement,” a  
series of elaborate notes onthe Epistles of St. Paul, some notes on  
/Eschylus, and a sufficient number of manuscript sermons to fill  
several volumes.  
  
A study of ‘‘ The Source of the ‘ Ancient Mariner,’ by Ivan  
James of South Wales University, is to be published at Curdiff.  
Mr. James argues that the source of the poem, of which Words-  
worth gave one version and De Quincey another, is to be found in  
the “strange and Dangerous Voyage of Captain Thomas James,”  
printed in London in 1633.

## [From _L'Univers_](http://data.theeuropeanlibrary.org/BibliographicResource/3000114042856)

#### 1893-04-26 &middot; [Paris](http://dbpedia.org/resource/Paris)

<table style="width: 100%;"><tr><td style="width: 50%">

avail de M. Gneist ost à coup sûf Tr£ téressant; mais il est gâté par l&#x27;injustice absolue que l&#x27;auteur manifeste de parti pris contre l&#x27;Eglise catholique, son rôle et ses défenseurs. Par exemple, en racontant les démêlés du Pape Innocent III aveo Jean- sans-Terre, il fait preuve d&#x27;une partialité flagrante. M. Gneist montre le même déplo rable esprit dans ce qu&#x27;il dit du rôle des jésuites, sous les deux derniers rois de la maison de Stuart. S&#x27;il ne présentait point ce grave défaut, le livre du professeur Gneist mériterait, par sa clarté et la science qu&#x27;il révèle, d&#x27;être placé à côté du célèbre Abrégé chronologi que de l&#x27;histoire et du droit public d&#x27;Alle magne, publié au siècle dernier par Ch. de Pfeffel, conseiller de légation français à la Diète de Ratisbonne. H. G. FROMM
</td></tr></table>

## [sim_saturday-review-uk_the-saturday-review-of-p_1894-07-28_78_2022](https://archive.org/details/sim_saturday-review-uk_the-saturday-review-of-p_1894-07-28_78_2022/page/n23/mode/1up?view=theater)

#### From unknown source

#### 1894-07-28

<table style="width: 100%;"><tr><td style="width: 50%">
